  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_74e7a554-28a2-48cf-bf92-01d1a4f83aab'
      });

  <span id="freeText5181665163425844009" style="display:none">Harriet Manners knows a lot of things. <br /><br />She knows that a cat has 32 muscles in each ear, a "jiffy" lasts 1/100th of a second, and the average person laughs 15 times per day. What she isn't quite so sure about is why nobody at school seems to like her very much. So when she's spotted by a top model agent, Harriet grabs the chance to reinvent herself. Even if it means stealing her Best Friend's dream, incurring the wrath of her arch enemy Alexa, and repeatedly humiliating herself in front of the impossibly handsome supermodel Nick. Even if it means lying to the people she loves. <br /><br />As Harriet veers from one couture disaster to the next with the help of her overly enthusiastic father and her uber-geeky stalker, Toby, she begins to realise that the world of fashion doesn't seem to like her any more than the real world did. <br /><br />And as her old life starts to fall apart, the question is: will Harriet be able to transform herself before she ruins everything?</span>

    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2006730708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15989576128854250705">This is exactly what I needed after reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11071466.Second_Chance_Summer' title='Second Chance Summer by Morgan Matson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Second Chance Summer</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are' title='Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Some Girls Are</a>- a fun, hilarious coming off age story. I felt like I laughed from start to finish. Harriet’s story could be compared to the Ugly Duckling’s except when Harriet transforms, she still ends up being herself and I thought that was great. She’s a certified geek from start to end and I loved that about the story. Although Harriet transforms, it’s mostly inner transformation. In the end, she earns self-confidence and r</span>
  <span id="freeText15989576128854250705" style="display:none">This is exactly what I needed after reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11071466.Second_Chance_Summer" title="Second Chance Summer by Morgan Matson" rel="nofollow noopener">Second Chance Summer</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are" title="Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Some Girls Are</a>- a fun, hilarious coming off age story. I felt like I laughed from start to finish. Harriet’s story could be compared to the Ugly Duckling’s except when Harriet transforms, she still ends up being herself and I thought that was great. She’s a certified geek from start to end and I loved that about the story. Although Harriet transforms, it’s mostly inner transformation. In the end, she earns self-confidence and realizes she’s great just the way she is. <br /><br />The plot may be a little bit unrealistic and some of the characters a bit stereotyped but they were all so fun to read and all of them managed to make me laugh. They’re all adorable and hilarious in their own ways. I don’t know but I find British humour really hilarious and relatable. <br /><br />I would highly recommend this book if you’re looking for a good contemporary that’ll make you laugh and feel good about yourself.</span>

<div id="review_686539053" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/686539053" />
    <a title="Laura Noakes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7474696-laura-noakes"><img alt="Laura Noakes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1450037031p2/7474696.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/686539053?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura Noakes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura Noakes" href="/user/show/7474696-laura-noakes">Laura Noakes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7474696-laura-noakes?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer686539053" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16675091050039949241">Ah. This book. I really had to mull over my feelings before writing a review because it wasn’t all horrible – there were some funny moments and some really heart-warming moments and I have to say that I thought it was written very well. But me and this book did not gel one iota.<br/><br/>First of all, Harriet. Harriet is our main character and self proclaimed ‘geek girl’. Harriet is meant to be fifteen, but she is more naïve then my thirteen year old sister. This was my first gripe. Harriet’s entire perso</span>
  <span id="freeText16675091050039949241" style="display:none">Ah. This book. I really had to mull over my feelings before writing a review because it wasn’t all horrible – there were some funny moments and some really heart-warming moments and I have to say that I thought it was written very well. But me and this book did not gel one iota.<br /><br />First of all, Harriet. Harriet is our main character and self proclaimed ‘geek girl’. Harriet is meant to be fifteen, but she is more naïve then my thirteen year old sister. This was my first gripe. Harriet’s entire personality seems to comprise of an endless list of facts. I really did not warm to her – I found her whiny and childish.<br /><br />Second of all, the plot. It didn’t feel timed right. The book seemed too short at times- the ending was rushed and yet at some points it dragged. And the love sub-plot had absolutely no development whatsoever which was very annoying.<br /><br />But my main issue with this book was its complete devolution from reality, and I am not talking about Harriet becoming a model – that does happen occasionally, but the environment – the school, the characters – they just did not seem real. I think this book is much more of a middle grade book then a YA, it caters to what twelve year olds think and dream about what happens when you’re a teenager and I have to say I think twelve year old me would have enjoyed it.<br /><br />I didn’t hate this book with a passion, but I was glad when I finished it and I don’t think I will be picking up the next book. It was just too fluffy for my tastes and I didn’t really like the main character.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16675091050039949241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28198445-ivana---diary-of-difference?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2568229355" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16199229658139905429"><a href='https://diaryofdifference.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blog</a> | <a href='https://www.facebook.com/diaryofdifference/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> | <a href='https://twitter.com/DiaryDifference' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> | <a href='https://www.instagram.com/diaryofdifference/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> | <a href='https://www.pinterest.co.uk/diaryofdifference/pins/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/>#1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13621089-geek-girl' rel='nofollow noopener'>Geek Girl</a> - ★★★★<br/>#1.5 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2942394177' rel='nofollow noopener'>Geek Girl: All Wrapped Up</a> - ★★★★<br/><br/>Even though I kept hearing great things about Geek Girl, I never really happened to read it. A month ago, my teen sister borrowed the whole Geek Girl series and told me this is something I must check off my list. And here I am one month later - loving the first book! <br/><br/>Geek Girl tells the story of a young teen Harriet, who is a geek and gets bullied at her school. She might know all the science</span>
  <span id="freeText16199229658139905429" style="display:none"><a href="https://diaryofdifference.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/diaryofdifference/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/DiaryDifference" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/diaryofdifference/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.co.uk/diaryofdifference/pins/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br /><br />#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13621089-geek-girl" rel="nofollow noopener">Geek Girl</a> - ★★★★<br />#1.5 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2942394177" rel="nofollow noopener">Geek Girl: All Wrapped Up</a> - ★★★★<br /><br />Even though I kept hearing great things about Geek Girl, I never really happened to read it. A month ago, my teen sister borrowed the whole Geek Girl series and told me this is something I must check off my list. And here I am one month later - loving the first book! <br /><br />Geek Girl tells the story of a young teen Harriet, who is a geek and gets bullied at her school. She might know all the science answers, but she has no clue why people are laughing at her when she goes outside with a cartoon hoodie. <br /><br />But when Harriet gets discovered by a modelling agency,she realises how things can get different, and she has to choose whether she wants to risk losing everything by changing who she really is.<br /><br />A very funny and geeky read, where I couldn’t stop but giggle a few times. One moment really got me though: <br /><br /><b>
  <i>‘’If somebody offers to shave your legs,’’ she snaps, ‘’let them.’’</i>
</b><br /><br />Harriet is a typical geeky high-school character, and you can’t help but love her weirdness, her silliness and the ways she believes in. <br /><br />The read was somewhat predictable from the very beginning, and there wasn’t any big plot twist or cliff-hanger, but I believe that this book didn’t really want to achieve that anyways. <br /><br />This was a perfect read for me to relax and enjoy reading - reminded me of my high-school days and made me remember a lot of similar moments. <br /><br />I am recommending it to all of you out there - that love being different and aren't afraid to stand up for yourselves, no matter how much people laugh at you.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_533815502" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/533815502" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413275441p2/10890208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/533815502?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=could-have-been-so-much-better">could-have-been-so-much-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=me-likes-you">me-likes-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=grinned-like-a-fool">grinned-like-a-fool</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer533815502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15772900719110832208">See more reviews at <a href='http://yamidnightreads.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>YA Midnight Reads</a><br/><br/><b>Thank you HarperCollins Australia for sending me this copy. No compensation was given or taken to alter this review. </b><br/><blockquote><br/>geek<br/>gi:k/<br/>informal<br/><i>noun</i><br/>noun: <b>geek</b>; plural noun: <b>geeks</b><br/> <br/>	 1. an unfashionable or socially inept person. <br/> <br/></blockquote><br/><div><br/><br/>Geek Girl is another one of those reads that have a bucket full of flaws, but is so entertaining and laid back that some of them just disappear. And that's totally cool every now and again. An imperfectly perfect novel.<br/><br/>Harriet Manners is a geek;</div></span>
  <span id="freeText15772900719110832208" style="display:none">See more reviews at <a href="http://yamidnightreads.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">YA Midnight Reads</a><br /><br /><b>Thank you HarperCollins Australia for sending me this copy. No compensation was given or taken to alter this review. </b><br /><blockquote><br />geek<br />gi:k/<br />informal<br /><i>noun</i><br />noun: <b>geek</b>; plural noun: <b>geeks</b><br /> <br />	 1. an unfashionable or socially inept person. <br /> <br /></blockquote><br /><div><br /><br />Geek Girl is another one of those reads that have a bucket full of flaws, but is so entertaining and laid back that some of them just disappear. And that's totally cool every now and again. An imperfectly perfect novel.<br /><br />Harriet Manners is a geek; even the <em>Oxford English Dictionary</em> is in complete agreement. Without a taste in fashion, one only friend and a brain full of unanticipated yet fun facts, Harriet pretty much ticks all the boxes. People at school tease her and when she thinks she's just about had enough of the four letter word appearing on her locker and bags, she's given the opportunity to transform herself. From geek, to modelling chic. An example of a flaw that soon vanished the more I read on was why did Harriet get spotted for a modelling job if she's supposedly, 'ugly'? Especially if her best and only friend, Nat, was prettier and wanted the job gazillion times more? We never get an explanation for this but eventually, who cares? I soon just got caught up in the humour and cuteness of the book.<br /><br />I would not say I loved Harriet like I had fore-expected. She's a geek, I'm a geek; we should have clicked from the get go. But...that wasn't exactly how it ended up to work. But let's start with the pros: I loved Harriet's inner dialogue; she's full of snark and humorous comments and some crazy awkward moments which I couldn't help but put a smile on my face. On the other hand, she got a little obsessively self-depreciating. I get it, you're not pretty and you don't get why you got the job. Blahblah. Tell me something new!<br /><br />Apart from our likable but sometimes annoying main character, the supporting characters were well created. Nat, Harriet's best friend was whole-heartedly honest and was a brilliant friend. She and Harriet got a little irritating with the amount of times where they'd fight over misunderstandings but still a great friendship dynamic. Harriet's relationship with her dad and step-mother, Annabel was also decent. I loved how Annabel and Harriet were really close and it got to the point where I thought Annabel was her birth-mother because they were so similar. Her dad was great as well though. And then we have Wilbur (that's bur, not iam) who was not my favourite. He never seemed to stick with the same nickname--and the nicknames were at times, puke worthy. Bleh. An eccentric man, he is. And then, we also have Toby, Harriet's personal geek stalker. He's kinda creepy but his interactions with Harriet were totally worth it. Talk about funny! What I didn't get is why Harriet could be so mean to Toby about him being a geek when she is one too. Then there's Alexa, who is a cliché pain in the ass and that's all I have to say about that shallow biatch. The minor plot line of a romance was a great addition. Seriously, Harriet and Nick were the cutest! It did border instant-love but, the slowly building chemistry was utterly worth it.<br /><br />Geek Girl is about being yourself and understanding that it's alright to be yourself. A great identity novel on a lazy day.</div></span>
  <a data-text-id="15772900719110832208" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_536189987" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/536189987" />
    <a title="Cora Tea Party Princess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4166936-cora-tea-party-princess"><img alt="Cora Tea Party Princess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548255984p2/4166936.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/536189987?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cora Tea Party Princess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cora Tea Party Princess" href="/user/show/4166936-cora-tea-party-princess">Cora Tea Party Princess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer536189987" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12164183197216961503"><b>5 Words: Hilarious, model, school, bullies, geeky.</b><br/><br/>I'd heard a lot about Geek Girl before I picked it up. I'd even bought it months beforehand. Even my none-bookish sister had read it and was raving about it and asking when I was getting the next book. I'd even started it, reading the first 15 chapters before my sister decided she'd like it better.<br/><br/>So I don't know why it took the book being picked as the Fashionista Book Club read for me to read it. Because I'd enjoyed the start, and I'd heard so </span>
  <span id="freeText12164183197216961503" style="display:none"><b>5 Words: Hilarious, model, school, bullies, geeky.</b><br /><br />I'd heard a lot about Geek Girl before I picked it up. I'd even bought it months beforehand. Even my none-bookish sister had read it and was raving about it and asking when I was getting the next book. I'd even started it, reading the first 15 chapters before my sister decided she'd like it better.<br /><br />So I don't know why it took the book being picked as the Fashionista Book Club read for me to read it. Because I'd enjoyed the start, and I'd heard so many good things.<br /><br />I think I didn't want to be disappointed.<br /><br />So thank goodness I wasn't!<br /><br />Geek Girl is fantastic. It's so so funny. I loved the relationship between Harriet and her parents, and how her dad and step-mum bickered all of the time. It was like reading my own parents and I loved it.<br /><br />I read each and every kooky fact out aloud to my other half. He usually hates it when I read out passages of books but with Geek Girl he even asked me what the most recent interesting fact was.<br /><br />Harriet's creepy stalker was a bit unbelievable, but on the whole this book was so real you could almost believe every word.<br /><br />And Wilbur was just a bit too much. He was too flowery, too garish. While the same thing worked for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2891665.Gail_Carriger" title="Gail Carriger" rel="nofollow noopener">Gail Carriger</a>'s Lord Akeldama, it didn't work so well for Wilbur. It was endearing, it was just annoying :(<br /><br />But this book was so so good, filled with wonderful facts and amazing writing and an uplifting plot that that didn't matter. It still gets a solid 5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12164183197216961503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1223775962" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9593762741755846355">Have you guys read this book yet? Oh man, it’s SO FUN! Let’s chat about it, shall we?<br/><br/><blockquote>“You need to stop caring what people who don’t matter think of you. Be who you are and let everybody else be who they are. Differences are a good thing.”</blockquote><br/><br/>Okay, let’s face it… most of us are geeks, right? Or at least have some geekish tendencies. I sure do. And I believe that’s why I loved this book so much. Harriet is the type of MC you can’t help but love. She’s such a stereotypical geek, but in the best possibl</span>
  <span id="freeText9593762741755846355" style="display:none">Have you guys read this book yet? Oh man, it’s SO FUN! Let’s chat about it, shall we?<br><br><blockquote>“You need to stop caring what people who don’t matter think of you. Be who you are and let everybody else be who they are. Differences are a good thing.”</blockquote><br><br>Okay, let’s face it… most of us are geeks, right? Or at least have some geekish tendencies. I sure do. And I believe that’s why I loved this book so much. Harriet is the type of MC you can’t help but love. She’s such a stereotypical geek, but in the best possible way. She knows she’s a geek, and though it’s not all fun and games, and outright torture at times, she completely accepts who she is and rolls with it. She doesn’t try to hide her geekness one bit. Right from the first page I couldn’t help loving Harriet. What a hoot!<br><br><blockquote>Our stories are drive by who we are and what we do, and not by the events that happens to us.</blockquote><br><br>This book was seriously funny. I laughed more than anything else while reading it. I had no idea the humor level would be so off the charts, so this was such a pleasant surprise. Though Harriet is facing some real serious things, she made the best of the situation at hand. She was naive and anxious and outright ridiculous at times, but she was real. I totally believed in her character and was routing for her the entire time. It wasn’t just Harriet that carried this story though. The secondary characters were magnificent! The cast of characters Harriet encounters while modeling were so much fun I couldn’t stop grinning. And Harriet’s father… seriously, he was just too much!<br><br><blockquote>“Oh.” Dad frowns. “Why hasn’t Annabel been teaching you how to walk in heels? I thought we had an agreement: I teach you how to be cool and she trains you how to be a girl.”<br><br>I stare at him in silence. This explains so much.”</blockquote><br><br><br>Geek Girl wasn’t all fun and games though. I loved the message it portrayed of being yourself, and not letting what others think of you change who you are on the inside. Such a wonderful message all wrapped up in the perfect little hilarious package. This was the kind of book I love so much, and I’m really looking forward to continuing on with this series. (That’s right, you read that correctly… I’m honestly and wholeheartedly looking forward to continuing on with a SERIES! There’s no question how much I loved these characters, huh? :D)<br><br>(<i>Thanks to HarperTeen for the review copy!</i>)<br><br><b>Find this review and others like it at <a href="http://lostinlit.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Lost in Literature!</a></b><br><p>
  <a href="http://www.lostinlit.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">

  </a>
</p><br></span>

<div id="review_1227074290" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1227074290" />
    <a title="Carlie K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28260702-carlie-k"><img alt="Carlie K" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481472798p2/28260702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1227074290?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carlie K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carlie K" href="/user/show/28260702-carlie-k">Carlie K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062333575" href="/book/show/22249710-geek-girl">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1227074290" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5990445307384208788">3.75 stars<br/>----------------------------------------------<br/>this review is originally posted on <a href='http://www.candythebookishgirl.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bookish Girl</a><br/>----------------------------------------------<br/>You can buy the book from <a href='http://www.bookdepository.com/Geek-Girl-Holly-Smale/9780062333575/?a_aid=thebookishgirl' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bookdepository</a><br/>----------------------------------------------<br/>A geek + a super model = Harriet Manners<br/><br/>The above equation is basically the synopsis of this book (*wink*) but I'll give you another version of it just in case you don't like Maths.<br/><br/>Harriet Manners is a full-time geek, which means she's the opposite of popular.</span>
  <span id="freeText5990445307384208788" style="display:none">3.75 stars<br />----------------------------------------------<br />this review is originally posted on <a href="http://www.candythebookishgirl.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bookish Girl</a><br />----------------------------------------------<br />You can buy the book from <a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/Geek-Girl-Holly-Smale/9780062333575/?a_aid=thebookishgirl" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookdepository</a><br />----------------------------------------------<br />A geek + a super model = Harriet Manners<br /><br />The above equation is basically the synopsis of this book (*wink*) but I'll give you another version of it just in case you don't like Maths.<br /><br />Harriet Manners is a full-time geek, which means she's the opposite of popular. One day, she gets spotted by an agent unexpectedly. In order to change for a better life, Harriet finally decides to start modeling in secret. But what she doesn't realize is that, modeling doesn't make her life better but hauls her into a great mess.<br /><br />I was taking a break from revision when I picked up this book, and the next thing I knew? I couldn't put it down and finished it in one sitting! The writing of Miss Smale is so easy to read and it brings me into Harriet's crazy world easily! I love that the chapters are super short so I actually flew though the book!<br /><br />For the characters, I think Miss Smale has done a great job on it. It's not common for me to like every single character in one book, but for this book, I truly do! Harriet is geeky and funny and dramatic! I never got bored with her humorous narration. I also love her childish yet loving dad, mature and clever stepmother, geeky and supportive stalker, loyal and amazing best friend. I even like the villain, which is very unusual for me. <br /><br />Moving on to the plot, I think it's pretty predictable, but there are a few plot details revealed at the end that I didn't see them coming (good job Miss Smale!). However, sometimes certain events lack for detailed descriptions and the love line is not strong enough. But since it's a debut novel, I expect to see improvements in the next few books and this book has the magic to make me want to continue with the series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5990445307384208788" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_520887315" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/520887315" />
    <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks"><img alt="Stacey (prettybooks)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577577052p2/3533262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/520887315?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey (prettybooks)" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks">Stacey (prettybooks)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17232242-geek-girl">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=read-in-my-twenties">read-in-my-twenties</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer520887315" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2655456345980831289">I'm going to a Geek Girl party this weekend, in which I'll be surrounded by many of my fellow UK book blogging friends, participating in a 'geek quiz', playing ping pong, and nibbling on snacks. As I don't particularly enjoy the slightly awkward feeling of attending a book event without having read the book (it feels a bit <em>fraudulent), </em>I decided to pick up <em>Geek Girl</em>. And I'm rather glad I did.<br/><br/><em>Geek Girl</em> is a fun, quirky roller-coaster I didn't see coming. A super quick read, it's the story of 15-</span>
  <span id="freeText2655456345980831289" style="display:none">I'm going to a Geek Girl party this weekend, in which I'll be surrounded by many of my fellow UK book blogging friends, participating in a 'geek quiz', playing ping pong, and nibbling on snacks. As I don't particularly enjoy the slightly awkward feeling of attending a book event without having read the book (it feels a bit <em>fraudulent), </em>I decided to pick up <em>Geek Girl</em>. And I'm rather glad I did.<br /><br /><em>Geek Girl</em> is a fun, quirky roller-coaster I didn't see coming. A super quick read, it's the story of 15-year-old Harriet Manners who goes from milquetoast to model in 60 seconds. You see, Harriet is a certified geek. She knows this because she looked it up in the <em>Oxford English Dictionary</em> sitting on her bedside table. Harriet has one friend (fashionista Nat) and one stalker (even geekier Toby), and everybody hates her. But<em> I</em> couldn't possibly understand why: Harriet's sparkling personality shines through from the very first page – I was hooked.<br /><br /><em>Geek Girl</em> shows us, if we didn't already know, that people with intelligence and 'unironic enthusiasm' (see: John Green), unfortunately, especially when they are teenagers, can sometimes fall subject to bullying, as Harriet discovers when archnemesis Alexa Roberts cruelly humiliates her in class. But is heading off to Russia to pursue a career in modelling the answer to all of popularity-challenged Harriet's problems?<br /><br />Aside from our protagonist, <em>Geek Girl</em> is full of wonderful and witty characters, a mix of the eccentric in <em>Ugly Betty</em> and smart and quick-witted in <em>Gilmore Girls</em>. From Annabell, Harriet's pinstripe suit-wearing stepmother and childish, overly enthusiastic father, to her wild fashion agent with a talent for turning any phrase into a charming nickname (How are you, sugar-kitten?). And yet is it uniquely British? Perhaps. I'd love to see whether the humour translates, because it's well worth experiencing. It's delightful and funny and silly, yet you'll learn some fantastic conversation-starters (or -stoppers, depending on who you're talking to) along the way. Did you know that bluebirds cannot see the colour blue?.<br /><br /><em>Geek Girl</em> is extremely exaggerated, dramatic, and extreme (although not entirely unrealistic as it is partly based on the author's own childhood), but I wouldn't have had it any other way. It's home to a host of articulate, well-constructed characters and is sure to delight geeks and nerd(fighters) alike!<br /><br /><i>Thank you HarperCollins Children's Books for providing this book for review!</i><br /><br /><i>edit: December 2013. I originally gave <i>Geek Girl</i> four stars, but after reading the sequel, I think I ought to have given it five so I have made that amendment!</i><br /><br /><i>I also reviewed this book over on <a href="http://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/book-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pretty Books</a>.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2655456345980831289" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1232518373" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1232518373" />
    <a title="Hazel (Stay Bookish)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5614985-hazel-stay-bookish"><img alt="Hazel (Stay Bookish)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405178063p2/5614985.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1232518373?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hazel (Stay Bookish)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hazel (Stay Bookish)" href="/user/show/5614985-hazel-stay-bookish">Hazel (Stay Bookish)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062333575" href="/book/show/22249710-geek-girl">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5614985-hazel-stay-bookish?shelf=own-physical-arc">own-physical-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5614985-hazel-stay-bookish?shelf=from-publishers">from-publishers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1232518373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6487479280980264991">Visit <a href='http://staybookish.net' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stay Bookish</a> for more book reviews!<br/><br/>Fun is the one perfect word I can think of that sums up Geek Girl. I picked it up on a pretty dull day and it easily put me in a happy mood as I laughed because of the hilarious MC and the delightful events that lead to her from being unpopular geek to becoming a model for a top UK fashion powerhouse as well as the events that occur after. Seriously, it was just such a fun book! Why? Let me list the reasons.<br/><br/>1. True to the title, Harriet Manners is a geek.</span>
  <span id="freeText6487479280980264991" style="display:none">Visit <a href="http://staybookish.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Stay Bookish</a> for more book reviews!<br /><br />Fun is the one perfect word I can think of that sums up Geek Girl. I picked it up on a pretty dull day and it easily put me in a happy mood as I laughed because of the hilarious MC and the delightful events that lead to her from being unpopular geek to becoming a model for a top UK fashion powerhouse as well as the events that occur after. Seriously, it was just such a fun book! Why? Let me list the reasons.<br /><br />1. True to the title, Harriet Manners is a geek. A really quirky geek at that. She likes rulers, dictionaries, history and organization. She’s awkward and very much socially inept. So authentic character? Check.<br /><br />2. With that, I found it really easy to connect with her.<br /><br />3. Harriet also occasionally makes lists which I really enjoyed because, if you must know, I love lists (if this list in itself wasn’t clue enough).<br /><br />4. It’s hard not to adore Harriet. She sometimes left me embarrassed for her but I couldn’t help but grin at how silly and ridiculous she and the story was. Her voice is ‘younger YA’ (rightfully so since she’s fifteen) so there tends to be exaggeration and long-winded dramatic story-telling but I actually found this totally amusing and endearing.<br /><br />5. The rest of the characters feel very animated- like the highly eccentric but super witty Wilbur and fellow geek and official stalker Toby.<br /><br />6. Present parents (dad and stepmom) who are also funny and even have an interesting subplot/arc of their own. I adore the dynamics in Harriet’s family and her very positive relationship with her stepmother.<br /><br />7. Although you’d initially think the plot is a bit unbelievable (which in this case you should know that it isn’t actually that much unrealistic, since the author experienced this herself), it felt concrete to me because I was just right there with Harriet. And it was fun riding along!<br /><br />8. We get a cute little budding romance here with Nick and Harriet. More please!<br /><br />9. But most importantly, the themes! Friendship, honesty, accepting who you are, overcoming bullies, staying true to yourself. Love it.<br /><br />With that, I’m really looking forward to the next books in the series! If you’re ready for a geeky cute (to the nth level) kind of book, definitely check Geek Girl out!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6487479280980264991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2756079165286530725">I had no idea how to rate this or even what to talk about when I finished this book. <br/><br/><i>Geek Girl</i> was a book that has been on my TBR for a while. Then when I saw it on my audible romance package - well, I went for it. However, I can't decide if it was the narrator, accent or just the MC that I didn't like. I mean, the story was okay and everything but other than that - I have no idea how I feel.<br/><br/>Harriet was cool and all but I don't see the problem with being a geek. She got bullied at school because</span>
  <span id="freeText2756079165286530725" style="display:none">I had no idea how to rate this or even what to talk about when I finished this book. <br /><br /><i>Geek Girl</i> was a book that has been on my TBR for a while. Then when I saw it on my audible romance package - well, I went for it. However, I can't decide if it was the narrator, accent or just the MC that I didn't like. I mean, the story was okay and everything but other than that - I have no idea how I feel.<br /><br />Harriet was cool and all but I don't see the problem with being a geek. She got bullied at school because of what she is - which again I don't see a problem with. One day she gets discovered by a modeling agency and her life kind of gets turned upside down. Unfortunately for her, she starts lying to everyone around her. Whether it's taking her best friends dreams and constantly telling her lies about this job OR it's her dad lying to her step mom about where they are.<br /><br />Eventually they get caught in the scheme of lying and shit kind of hits the fan. Throughout the whole modeling career of hers, she thinks everything is going change for her. Nope, her life doesn't drastically get better at school. She still gets bullied BUT she is making a career for herself. Yeah, she likes modeling but it comes at a price for her. <br /><br />Overall, it was a cute book. I honestly thought at the end she was going to try and get her friend a modeling job but she didn't. </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer1069888270460324156">Love. So much love.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>What worked:</u>
</b> Officially one of my new favourite series. Seriously. It’s up there with Delirium, Chronicles of Narnia, Kate Daniels and Georgia Nicholson! When I first saw Geek Girl, I was expecting something fluffy and light that I could absorb into my brain. Did I get that? Yes. But what else did I get from it? I got my geek on, I learned new facts that I can throw at my friends, I found a kindred spirit. Holly Smale, can we be best friends?<br/><br/>I can barely write a coherent r</span>
  <span id="freeText1069888270460324156" style="display:none">Love. So much love.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>What worked:</u>
</b> Officially one of my new favourite series. Seriously. It’s up there with Delirium, Chronicles of Narnia, Kate Daniels and Georgia Nicholson! When I first saw Geek Girl, I was expecting something fluffy and light that I could absorb into my brain. Did I get that? Yes. But what else did I get from it? I got my geek on, I learned new facts that I can throw at my friends, I found a kindred spirit. Holly Smale, can we be best friends?<br /><br />I can barely write a coherent review because that is how much this book rocked my world. I could waffle on for quite a while but all you’d see would be fangirling and lots of exclamation marks. Instead, this review is for you. What do you want to see in this book?<br /><br />Would you like awesome parents that have the most hilarious tiffs? Would you like an agent that is so fabulous he must be found and taken shopping? Would you like a love interest that you can swoon over? Would you like a female protagonist that will warm the cockles of your heart with her accident-prone ways, her cute stalker and her utter geekiness? Then have at it, get this book!<br /><br /><b>
  <u>What irked:</u>
</b> Not a thing, nope, you won’t take my love away from me.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Recommended to:</u>
</b> Everyone! From staunch Chick-Lit lovers to the most hardcore of nerds. From galaxies far, far away to the launderette down the road. I’d give this book …***5 Stars – My mind is in bits on the floor, that’s how good this book is.***</span>

<div id="review_530756490" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/530756490" />
    <a title="Samina The Story Devourer " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3974718-samina-the-story-devourer"><img alt="Samina The Story Devourer " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416918256p2/3974718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/530756490?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samina The Story Devourer " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samina The Story Devourer " href="/user/show/3974718-samina-the-story-devourer">Samina The Story Devourer </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3974718-samina-the-story-devourer?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3974718-samina-the-story-devourer?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer530756490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5779992253267095632"><b>My ratings: 4.5 out of 5 stars</b><br/><br/><br/>Before I go nose diving into my review, I have a confession to make. I’m a geek. Let’s make a big massive GEEK. In fact I’m pretty sure I’m Harriett Manners. Or perhaps Harriett is modelled after every Geek girl out there. Harriett was so real to me. It felt like story was being told. Well, I’m not exactly model material but I’d like to think I am.<br/><br/>Harriett is your average geek girl next door, complete with a fashion crazy best friend and a geeky stalker. She was you</span>
  <span id="freeText5779992253267095632" style="display:none"><b>My ratings: 4.5 out of 5 stars</b><br /><br /><br />Before I go nose diving into my review, I have a confession to make. I’m a geek. Let’s make a big massive GEEK. In fact I’m pretty sure I’m Harriett Manners. Or perhaps Harriett is modelled after every Geek girl out there. Harriett was so real to me. It felt like story was being told. Well, I’m not exactly model material but I’d like to think I am.<br /><br />Harriett is your average geek girl next door, complete with a fashion crazy best friend and a geeky stalker. She was your quintessenscail geek girl who hasn’t got a clue about fashion, boys and is utterly socially inept. She keeps sprouting random bits of information which may be interesting (of, course I find them interesting) to the dismay of the people around her.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Our stories are driven by who we are and what we do, not by the events that happen to us."</i>
</b><br /><br />One day Harriett gets scouted when her BFF was meant to scouted. Finally fed up being treated as the underdog, against the wishes of her step mother and at the risking of losing every one she love Harriett decided to go ahead and be a model.<br /><br />A geek trying to be a model? I had to read this book. I mean I try really hard these not so it’s not too obvious but I’m a geek. It felt like a personal Cinderella story too. I loved loved loved Harriett. From her dorky clothes to her random bit of info dropping, it was all so endearing. She was so cute that I wanted to take this version of Mimi-me home.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"....stop caring what people who don’t matter think of you. Be who you are and let everybody else be who they are. Differences are a good thing. It would be a terribly boring world if we were all the same.” </i>
</b><br /><br />The story line was quick and fast moving. I loved the side characters which added flavour to this sweet story of coming of age. I loved Harriett’s dad. It would suck to have a dad who would embarrass you every day but it would be great to know a grown up as fun as him. I even enjoyed the geeky Toby who simply would not stop stalking Harriett.<br /><br />Geek Girl was fun, peppy and adventurous. Yes I said adventurous. It felt like one. Harriett going away on photo shoots and stumbling her way around the fashion world is nothing but an adventure. How would a geek (insert *me*) find her way in the treacherous waters filled with meat eating sharks, ready to snap a bite off you?<br /><br />Okay, I think I may be getting carried away here. Ahem, this treacherous world may seem terrifying for me Harriett but the story had enough pretty to motivate me. Nick was...let’s just say interesting. He was handsome, charming, clever, witty, and elusive and to make matters worse, mysterious. I had no chance. I mean, Harriet had no chance.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Nobody really metamorphoses. Cinderella is always Cinderella, just in a nicer dress. The Ugly duckling was always a swan, just a smaller version. And I bet the tadpole and the caterpillar still the same, even when they’re jumping and flying, swimming and floating. Just like I am.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Over all, Geek Girl was fun and light reading. The side characters interesting and it doesn’t hurt that in Victorian time women used to use dead mice skin as a fashion accessory or that the water doesn’t reflect the sky but reflects the wave length of the colour blue. I enjoyed this book immensely and it might not have left a long lasting impression on me but I’m sure I can pick this book a year later and still enjoy. Highly recommended to all geek self-confessed or not.<br /><br /><i>Arc provided by HarperCollins UK.</i><br /><br />Read more of my reviews at <a href="www.escapismfromreality.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Escapism from Reality</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5779992253267095632" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3695511110261542012">Meet <b>Harriet Manners</b> -- our resident 15 y/o geek girl.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I'm not a big fan of the colour red, even if it is the longest wavelength of light discernible by the human eye."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Well, my fave color is red, and I didn't know that.<br/><br/>Let me tell you, I feel pretty giddy whenever I start a book. I believe that no book can be so bad that it doesn't contain even a single new knowledge or information.<br/><br/>Fortunately, this book is full of them. I'm seriously learning lots of actual trivias while reading thi</span>
  <span id="freeText3695511110261542012" style="display:none">Meet <b>Harriet Manners</b> -- our resident 15 y/o geek girl.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I'm not a big fan of the colour red, even if it is the longest wavelength of light discernible by the human eye."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Well, my fave color is red, and I didn't know that.<br /><br />Let me tell you, I feel pretty giddy whenever I start a book. I believe that no book can be so bad that it doesn't contain even a single new knowledge or information.<br /><br />Fortunately, this book is full of them. I'm seriously learning lots of actual trivias while reading this YA goodie -- now, that's a first.<br /><br />Because this book dragged a bit at times, I don't think this could be read in one sitting. Took me almost a month and other good books in between to finish this one. But whenever I pick it up again, I found myself enjoying the few chapters. Nothing beats good humor in an uneventful day.<br /><br />The only thing that irritates me the most was the varied terms of endearment used by the top model agent, <b>Wilbur</b>.<br /><br /><i>Petal, Sponge-finger, Chocolate-drops, Baby-baby Unicorn.</i><br /><br />Like, <b><i>seriously</i>???</b> He must have called Harriet a hundred different names throughout the book!<br /><br />First off, I have nothing against the gay community. I don't even know how fashion mavens talk but I thought Wilbur's personality was so exaggerated it's NOT even funny. In fact, whenever I read about Wilbur's line, I feel like pulling my hair out. It's just so annoying!!<br /><br />Thank goodness, I let that out.<br /><br />~<i>This book was provided by the publisher via NetGalley in exhange for an honest review.</i></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer477806278" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2496518882456409304">This review can also be found on my blog: <a href='http://amatchmadeinheavenreviews.blogspot.ca/2013/02/geek-girl-by-holly-smale-geek-girl-1.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Match Made in Heaven</a><br/><br/><a href='http://imgur.com/q0Rf4Hu' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400899i/777394.jpg' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>This was a typical coming-of-age story. Very predictable. Harriet is picked on in school and when she is offered a modelling job, she accepts hoping it will change her life for the better. But she soon realizes that there are bullies wherever you go, and the trick is to ignore them, be yourself, and remember what is really important. <br/><br/>This was very brief. I read it in two sittings, and not much really happened. Her modeling caree</span>
  <span id="freeText2496518882456409304" style="display:none">This review can also be found on my blog: <a href="http://amatchmadeinheavenreviews.blogspot.ca/2013/02/geek-girl-by-holly-smale-geek-girl-1.html" rel="nofollow noopener">A Match Made in Heaven</a><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/q0Rf4Hu" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400899i/777394.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This was a typical coming-of-age story. Very predictable. Harriet is picked on in school and when she is offered a modelling job, she accepts hoping it will change her life for the better. But she soon realizes that there are bullies wherever you go, and the trick is to ignore them, be yourself, and remember what is really important. <br><br>This was very brief. I read it in two sittings, and not much really happened. Her modeling career consisted of one photoshoot, one catwalk, and one interview. It took up a very small part of the book. Most of the book focused on her home life and her relationship with her best friend, Nat. Harriet was not a real geek, but a nerd. Maybe the lingo is different in the UK. But for me, a geek is a person interested in pop culture, sci-fi, fantasy, anime, books, comics, cosplay, etc. A nerd is a person who is extremely smart and enjoys school and studying, and stereotypically has glasses and is socially awkward. That is Harriet. She is quirky and I appreciated her character. There was a bit of humour between her and her adorable stalker, Toby. <br><br>There was also a barely-there romance. We know absolutely nothing about Harriet's love interest besides the fact that he is gorgeous, part Asian, and he likes Harriet. There isnt a lot of depth in this. Its definitely for a younger audience, perhaps middle grade, who would perhaps appreciate the simple message of the story: Be yourself.<br><br><i>ARC provided by NetGalley on behalf of HarperCollins, in exchange for an honest review.</i></span>

<div id="review_1009343600" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1009343600" />
    <a title="AH" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3255548-ah"><img alt="AH" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275413869p2/3255548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1009343600?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AH" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AH" href="/user/show/3255548-ah">AH</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062333575" href="/book/show/22249710-geek-girl">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=arc-edelweiss">arc-edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=blue">blue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=zzread-jan2015">zzread-jan2015</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1009343600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11970018694022923618">Woo hoo! First book read in 2015!<br/><br/><b>Geek Girl</b> was a surprisingly quick and entertaining read. Our heroine Harriet was both lovable and sweet and so geeky and adorable. Harriet has always lived in the periphery - she often feels like a "polar bear in the rain forest," which may or may not be a good thing. Harriet often finds herself in all sorts of wacky situations and her primary coping mechanism is to dive under a table and hide. While on a field trip to Birmingham, Harriet is discovered by a larg</span>
  <span id="freeText11970018694022923618" style="display:none">Woo hoo! First book read in 2015!<br /><br /><b>Geek Girl</b> was a surprisingly quick and entertaining read. Our heroine Harriet was both lovable and sweet and so geeky and adorable. Harriet has always lived in the periphery - she often feels like a "polar bear in the rain forest," which may or may not be a good thing. Harriet often finds herself in all sorts of wacky situations and her primary coping mechanism is to dive under a table and hide. While on a field trip to Birmingham, Harriet is discovered by a large modeling agency and made the fresh new face of Baylee. A gawky girl in high heels, stumbling, much like she stumbles through life. But there is an endearing grace to Harriet that makes you fall in love with her. <br /><br />I liked that Harriet was not one of those cookie cutter drop dead gorgeous girls. Harriet struggles and stumbles through life - her arch-nemesis Alexa bullies and humiliates her to no end, her beautiful best friend Nat dreams of becoming a model, and she is "stalked" by Toby, who adores her. Harriet is brilliant, but her social skills are a little lacking. I think that what I loved about this book was the actual inclusion of parental figures - Harriet's father and stepmother offered Harriet some stability and love. <br /><br /><b>Geek Girl</b> was an enjoyable read, full of hilarious moments. I'm looking forward to reading more books by this author in the future.<br /><br /><i>Thank you to Edelweiss and HarperTeen for a review copy of this book. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></i></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16579490745549671078">Read: January 2018<br/>Rating: 3.5/5 stars<br/><br/><i>Geek Girl</i> was on a long list of books my teenage daughter has recommended that I read, and I can see why she likes it. Harriet is a quirky, likeable protagonist and the plot is entertaining and easy to follow. I especially like the fact that Harriet has a loving and healthy relationship with her dad and step-mother. <br/><br/>The only reason this was not a four star read was that the plot became more and more unrealistic towards the end of the novel; there's no way <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(vi</a></span>
  <span id="freeText16579490745549671078" style="display:none">Read: January 2018<br />Rating: 3.5/5 stars<br /><br /><i>Geek Girl</i> was on a long list of books my teenage daughter has recommended that I read, and I can see why she likes it. Harriet is a quirky, likeable protagonist and the plot is entertaining and easy to follow. I especially like the fact that Harriet has a loving and healthy relationship with her dad and step-mother. <br /><br />The only reason this was not a four star read was that the plot became more and more unrealistic towards the end of the novel; there's no way <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Harriet would still be asked to sign another modelling contract after humiliating the fashion industry live on TV! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="16579490745549671078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2047275788" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2047275788" />
    <a title="Dawnie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36293066-dawnie"><img alt="Dawnie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464172620p2/36293066.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2047275788?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dawnie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dawnie" href="/user/show/36293066-dawnie">Dawnie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36293066-dawnie?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36293066-dawnie?shelf=library-book">library-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2047275788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2699006027593211517">This was fun and easy and what i expect it to be with the amount of overdone fluff, grin worthy lines and completely overdone "joke" moments. <br/><br/>It clearly is a book targeted towards younger girls and i knew that going in and it was what i wanted: something silly and fun and easy to read and this book is exactly that!<br/><br/>I enjoyed that Harriet is actually a smart and "geeky" girl that enjoys learning and learning facts that you will never ever need in "real" life (which i could relate really well to be</span>
  <span id="freeText2699006027593211517" style="display:none">This was fun and easy and what i expect it to be with the amount of overdone fluff, grin worthy lines and completely overdone "joke" moments. <br /><br />It clearly is a book targeted towards younger girls and i knew that going in and it was what i wanted: something silly and fun and easy to read and this book is exactly that!<br /><br />I enjoyed that Harriet is actually a smart and "geeky" girl that enjoys learning and learning facts that you will never ever need in "real" life (which i could relate really well to being a person myself that loves learning and knowing stupid little things that are just fun to know)<br /><br />Most of the characters where enjoyable and i did like that the stepmother was a great mother and that she was a smart woman -the smart parent!- and that she tried to talk Harriet out of becoming a model. Can't explain why that was because that would take forever, but i just liked that a mother tried to stop her daughter from modelling instead of being the parent that pushes her into it. <br /><br />I do have to say that both Toby and Harriets father where over done in those books, the "stalker" was a bit too extreme with the constant popping up literary out of nowhere and just knowing where Harriet was, thats a bit too strange in my option. And Harriets father was just a bit too much of a "fun" parent, of an over extreme character that felt like a little brother doing stupid things in the background instead of a father figure. And i kind of hate when authors take those easy ways with parents of a story instead of making them actual real parents. <br /><br />What i also didn't love about this book is that at the beginning of this book and quiet a few times throughout it, its often stated that Harriet is not the prettiest girl. Which is fine especially since most models -in my option!- are not necessary the most beautiful people, but i just think its a bit strange that we are so often told that the best friend Nat is this beautiful girl and Harriet apparently is the exact opposite of that and than the "ugly" girl gets the modelling job? Does that just make no sense at all to me? I just think that the author over did it a bit with the Harriet is "ugly" thing. I would have preferred it it would have just been said that Harriet wasn't the most beautiful, but that she was simply a normal looking girl. That would have just made more sense to me, especially with the modelling factor added in. But thats a personal thing, but since it is my personal review i am mentioning it!!<br /><br /><b> Overall this book was good, and if you are not a reader between 10 to 16 years old (since they will surely enjoy this easy and fun to read book if they like this type of book) and you want to read something fun and easy and completely silly book? Go for it! </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="2699006027593211517" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14922378221751598353"><b> doesn't anyone write honest reviews these days? can't believe this book is so well accepted so far. </b><br/><br/>Simply appalling. Nothing good to say about this book. No plot, not at all interesting or original themes, unreal and ridiculous relationships and zero character development, annoying characters and a pseudo intellectual heroine who really is an imbecile. Being in her head hurt my brain, I thought the narration was awful and unnatural.. so this book was just icky for me. Maybe if I was a mediocre</span>
  <span id="freeText14922378221751598353" style="display:none"><b> doesn't anyone write honest reviews these days? can't believe this book is so well accepted so far. </b><br /><br />Simply appalling. Nothing good to say about this book. No plot, not at all interesting or original themes, unreal and ridiculous relationships and zero character development, annoying characters and a pseudo intellectual heroine who really is an imbecile. Being in her head hurt my brain, I thought the narration was awful and unnatural.. so this book was just icky for me. Maybe if I was a mediocre uninspired pre-teen of lower intellect..? But doubtful after all.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Oy9IkCzUQMcmHWbZfIQvKwReen4YrTYjtv0jcN1/D2+W6A6lVzxITr/vWwYrSDfvC/wuSw/lgkd+YYXjTzhiOg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dS+jmArNvzR8zBV1o1TppRZFxqZniqeq9RQfd3JIEoDY6OWtcSW3veU+KKr0mPFhGeeSk3DCE849iLnk4A9/1Q==')})
  }
//]]>

  <span id="freeText9403752478526058242" style="display:none">Holly is the Number One bestselling, multi-award winning author of the GEEK GIRL series. <br /><br />She fell in love with writing at five years old, when she realised that books didn't grow on trees like apples. A passion for travel, adventure and wearing no shoes has since led her all over the world: she has visited 27 countries, spent two years working as an English teacher in Japan, volunteered in Nepal, been bartered for in Jamaica and had a number of ear-plugs stolen in Australia, Indonesia and India.<br /><br />Holly has a BA in English Literature, an MA in Shakespeare, and currently lives in London or at @holsmale. <br /><br />The GEEK GIRL series has been an internationally bestselling no1. smash-hit. It won the Waterstones Teen Prize of the Year and the Leeds book award, was shortlisted for the Roald Dahl Funny Prize and the Branford Boase award, and was long-listed for the Carnegie.</span>
